The best open-source Excel alternativeâ€”based on stability, feature richness, and compatibilityâ€”is **LibreOffice Calc**.

### ğŸ”§ Why LibreOffice Calc?
- **Free & Open Source**: No subscriptions, ads, or limitations.
- **High Compatibility**: Opens `.xls`, `.xlsx`, `.csv`, and more with solid fidelity.
- **Advanced Features**: Supports pivot tables, macros, charts, functions, and conditional formatting.
- **Actively Maintained**: Backed by The Document Foundation with frequent updates.
- **Offline Ready**: Full-featured without needing internet access.

---

### ğŸŸ¢ Other Notable Mentions:
| Name                | Pros | Cons |
|---------------------|------|------|
| **OnlyOffice**      | Modern UI, good MS compatibility | Heavier RAM usage |
| **Gnumeric**        | Lightweight, fast | Fewer features |
| **EtherCalc**       | Collaborative (web-based) | Very basic features |
| **Calligra Sheets** | KDE integration, decent UI | Lower compatibility with Excel formats |

---

### ğŸš€ Recommendation:
Use **LibreOffice Calc** if you're doing serious spreadsheet work and want reliability. Itâ€™s what Iâ€™d use if I were running local ops, especially in a lightweight or decentralized environment.

### ğŸ§  **Best Practices**:

**assistant:**

Perfect call. Inkscape is powerful for thisâ€”open source and precise.

Hereâ€™s a clear, efficient way to structure your **Inkscape master document** for multi-size Google Ads production:

---

### ğŸ§° Step-by-Step Setup for Google Ads in Inkscape

#### 1. **Set Document Size**
Set the overall document size to the **largest ad size youâ€™ll produce**, which is:

- **300Ã—600 px** (Half Page) â† Set this as the document size.

This ensures nothing gets clipped and allows full visibility of all layers/artboards.

---

#### 2. **Create Named Layers for Each Ad Size**

Create one layer per ad size:
- `Layer_300x250`
- `Layer_728x90`
- `Layer_300x600`
- `Layer_320x100`
- `Layer_336x280`

Each layer will act like a virtual â€œartboard.â€

---

#### 3. **Draw Guides or Rectangles for Each Ad Frame**

On each layer:
- Create a **rectangle** at the corresponding size.
- Name the rectangle or group with the size (e.g., `frame_300x250`).
- Use a visible stroke color (no fill) for guide reference.
- Place it top-left (or anywhere that doesn't overlap) and keep each frame contained within its bounds.

This lets you toggle layers and export precisely.

---

#### 4. **Design Within Each Frame**
- Toggle only one layer visible at a time.
- Build your design elements inside the rectangle frame.
- Align text, images, and buttons with mobile/desktop readability in mind.

---

#### 5. **Exporting**
To export each size:

- **Select the rectangle** for the size you're exporting.
- Use `File â†’ Export PNG Image â†’ Selection` and make sure resolution is **96 DPI** (default) or adjust if needed.
- Name your files like:
  - `HOK_300x250_VariantA.png`
  - `HOK_728x90_VariantB.png`
- Keep file sizes under **150KB** for Google Ads.

---

### ğŸ” Bonus Tips

- **Use Clipping Masks** to keep artwork inside each frame.
- **Keep fonts legible at small sizes** (14px+ recommended).
- Consider **exporting test drafts at 2Ã— size** for previewing clarity, then export final at 1Ã—.

---
